EA training should be provided to irrigation users associations and DGRNR. in
addition, regional offices of DINAMA should be formally incorporated to local irrigation
boards (jmtas de riego).
9.    Public ParticiDation
The approach proposed for dealing with environmental aspects has been discussed
with all relevant govenmnent agencies (DGRNR, DINAMA, DH, OPP, OSE and University
UNICEM) and with a range of NGOs including the Rice Growers Association, Red de
Ecologia Social, Sociedad de Conservaci6n del Medio Ambiente, Amigos de la Preservaci6n
Ambiental and the consortium AGUAS grouping ten conservation associations organized
mainly to promote protection of the eastern wetlands of the country. A number of meetings
were held mainly in agencies and NGOs headquarters and, in some cases, in PRENADER
offices, during June, November and December 1992.
When considering the environmental profiles of specific projects, the respective
project propo? 's were discussed with the involved individual f4*rmers or farmer orgaztions
(CADYL, JTMECAL). Copies of the preliminary project proposals were circulated for
comments to four environmental NGOs (APA, SCMA, ITM and AGUAS). So far, no
objections have been raised on environmental or other grounds by these NGOs.
10.  Enironmental Procedures under the Loan. Within the project cycle seven steps
will be taken to assure that environmental issues are adequately considered in the selection,
design, construction and O&M of irrigation schemes.
(a)   Scheme proposals prepared by the boards of irrigation for submission to the
Inter-Ministerial Coordinating Council (CCI) will include a statement on
potential enviromnental implications (SPE) based on a check-list approved by
DINAMA and DGRNR.
(b)   For schemes approved for feasibility study by the CCI, an environmental
profile will be prepared for purposes of classifying their potential
environmental impact: "A" requiring a full-scale EA; "B" requiring further
study of specific aspects; or "C" requiring no further environmental studies.
These profiles will be prepared by the UEP in consultation with DGRNR and
DINAMA.
(c) Profiles will be submitted for comment to relevant units of MTOP, OPP and
MGAP, local groups affected by the project, and the NGOs concenmed with
these issues. The qualification of NGOs to be asked to comment would be
based on the criteria used by DINAMA for routine consultations with groups
outside the Government.
(d)   Observations from these enities (point c) would be submitted to the USP
which would be responsible for revision of the profiles, in association with
DGRNR, DH and DINAMA. the revised profiles together with a report on



-167-                              Annex M
the external consultations, would be submitted to CCI for final decision on the
environmental classification (point b).
(e)   In case of 'A" or "B" classification, CCI would require the UEP to draw up
terms of reference, in association with DINAMA, and contract the necessary
studies to assess potendal environmental impact and to produce
recommendations for mitigatory measures and M&E. These suxdies will be
financed under PRENADER; funding for the studies will be provided tirough
the UEP budget.
(f)   The EA studies would be circulated for information to all entities consulted on
the profiles and would be taken into account by CCI in detrmiing the final
design and ultimate eligibility of schemes to be recommended to the Bank for
finacing under the loan.
(g)   At the stages of construcion and O&M, CCI, through the DGRNR and DH,
would be responsible for the implementation of recommended mitigatory
meawres and M&E of impacts. This process will be directly supported by
four other program components:
(i) The research activity, exeuted by the National Agricultural Research
Institute (INIA) which includes the aspects related to potential
contamination of ground and surface water from agrochemicals and soil
degradation under intensive irrigated agriculture.
(-i) The study of water quality affecting and affected by irrigation under the
direction of DGRNR, DH and the National Directorate of Mining and
Geology (DINAMIGE).
(iii) The DGRNR program for extension of soil conservation techniques.
(iv) The study of micro watersheds, the Commission for the Development
of the Santa Lucia Basin (CHDCRSL).
11.   With respect to candidate schemes in the "area of influence" of the wetlands in the

considered within the 325,000 ha Ramsar Treaty area (not including the
Umguayan Merim Lagoon water surface), and projects likely to influence the
water regime within the above area wil be subject to rigorous EA.
(b)   The same conditions as in point (a) would apply to any areas of the 140,000
ha wedand reserve which may faU outside the Ramsar Treaty limits (parm 6).
(c)   Once the Ramsar limits are officially modified the rles in points (a) and (b)
wiUl apply to the new area.

1.    During the first two years of the project, supervision efforts would focus on
organization, team development, and operational issues (i.e., procurement, disbursement, and

Bank procedures and responsibilities. In summary, during the first phase of the project,
supervision missons will concentrate on providing the necessary assistance to the Borrower
to facilitate project implementation.
2.   It is expected that Bank supervision missions will assist UEP and the project
executing agencies (MGAP and MTOP) in prioritizing public investments as well as human
resource allocation. Selection of consultants will require special attention in order to ensure
the technical, financial, and environmental soundness of the proposed investments.
Strengthening of local managerial capacity and active beneficiary participation in design and
implementation of I&D schemes will ensure continuity of the project.
3.    Selection of consultants for the basic studies (i.e., Raig6n, and Salto aquifers, and
economic/environmental assessment for the Water Harvesting "Pilot" Program), as well as
assisig the Borrower in the preparation of bidding documents for procurement of works and
equipment, wiU be major tasks to be carried out during the first year of project
implementaton.
4.    Given the programmatic approach of the project, performance of all activities will be
carefully reassessed during implementation. Along these lines, project performance
indicators will be reviewed during the amual and mid-term reviews to ensure relevance and
that development impact ratings adequately reflect project objectives.

Annual and Mid-Term Reviews
6.    Annual reviews would take place by March-April of each year starting in 1994, and
the mid-term review in June 1996 (FY96). Both the annual reviews and mid-term review
would entail an itemized analysis by project component (i.e., Natural Resource Management,
and rigation Development) against the project implementation and impact indicators (Annex
0), as well as an assessment of the Government's subsector strategy. Both exercises would
also assess the appropriateness of skill mix and financial support at the level of UEP and
executing agencies (MGAP and MTOP), and their association with the policy decision level
(Ierministerial Coordinating Committee). An assessment of the design and implementation
of the government's natural resource management strategy, as well as enforcement of capital
cost recovery and O&M policy, will provide a qualitative measure of project impact.
Accordingly, and based on the results of the analysis, the annual and mid-term reviews
would offer the opporunity to adjust project implementation as appropriate, in light of actual
experience.

for an expansion of and possible adjustments to the training and
technical assistance program would be defined;
(v) institutional Strengthening: Review of sector institutions and
performance and their ability to undertake sector analysis relevant to
program and policy decisions, as well as the capacity and effectiveness
of the emecuting agencies' to monitor project implementation. Assess
content and design of the training and technical assistance program
(Annex P), including level of attendance/participation and impact on the
performance of local technical staff and farmers. The proposed
approach and objectives of each phase of TA and training would also



- 172 -                            Annex N
be assessed. Improvements in budgeting anid financial management
practices, organization and team development, and strengthening and
delegation of furnions at the regional level would be evaluated during
the project implementation reviews;
(vi) Natural Resource Management Studies: Analyze the results of the
proposed baseline studies (SAR para. 2.19) as technical input to the
definition of policy in the program areas (i.e., soil and water resource
management/conservation). Determine the extent to which the results
of the proposed studies have crystallized on specific policy guidelines
and actions, and stimulate the private sector to improve water use
efficiency and adopt natural resource conservation practices; and
(vii)  Fore=rv Development: Overall impact of the project on improved
forest resource management and conservation measured by the level of
adoption of new technologies. Review progress, scope, and possible
adjustments of the proposed technical assistance and taining program
in light of the experience gained under Ln 3131-UR.
(b)   Irigation Development
(i)  Rehabilitation and Modernization of Existing I&D Schemes: Review of
technical design and specifications of the proposed I&D schemes to
ensure compliance with engineering standards and agreed conditions,
including an evaluation of the level of acceptance (and enforcement) of
capital cost recovery and O&M agreements signed between the
Goverment and water users. An evaluation of the regulatory and
administrative framework implemented under the project, as it affects
private investment and improves water resource allocation and
efficiency, would also be carried out during the annual and mid-term
reviews. Based on the result of the analysis, possible adjustments
would be recommended, as necessary. Implememtion arrangements
(i.e., procurement procedures, technical assistance and training
schedule, availability of counterpart funding, and beneficiary
participation in the design and operation of the proposed investments)
would be assessed;
(ii) New Medium-Size I&D Schemes and Small Farmer Irrigation
Infiasitrure: As defined in para. (i) above. In addition, the anmual
and mid-term reviews would evaluate actual demand measured against
projections made at appraisal (SAR, paras. 2.26, 2.27, and 2.29) and
eligibility criteria utilized for the selection of I&D schemes financed
under the project. Adjustments to the proposed investment plan would
be made, as needed. Appropriateness and implementation of capital
cost recovety and O&M policy would be assessed. Special attention
will be given to the technical soundness and timeliness of EA impact
studies. Overall, the evaluation of the Irrigation Development



- 173 -                            Annex N
component would be made following a watershed management
approach;
(iii) Water Harvesting Pilot Pr gram: The analysis would focus on the
results of the environmental/economic assessment study quantifying the
externalities associated with the systematic development of small water
catchments (earthfills) within the selected pilot area. Actual demand
and beneficiary participation and commitment to the proposed capital
cost recovery policy would be assessed. Possible adjustments to the
investment targets established at appraisal would be considered, as
appropriate; and
(iv) Non-Traditional Export Crop Promotion: Implementation of the
proposed technical assistance and training program would be contingent
upon the result of an in-depth impact assessment of the PENTA
program financed under Loan 3131-UR, to be carried out at the mid-
term review in June 1996.
(c)   Project Management
(i)  UEP performance: UEP would be evaluated with major emphasis on
its ability to coordinate and assist sector institutions to achieve the
project's objectives. UEP responsibility will include, among others:
consolidation of Annual Operating Plans (POAs), follow-up compliance
with inter-agency cooperation agreements, financial management
inciuding allocation and monitoring of project funds, and availability of
counterpart funding. The composition (skill mix) of the UEP will be
analyzed in order to receive feedback from the executing agencies
regarding the unit's ability to adequately coordinate and manage
technical, administrative, and financial issues;
(ii)  Procurement and Disbursements: Technical ability, soundness of
judgment, and compliance with Bank guidelines will be assessed takdng
into account acual project performance during the period under review.
The analysis will indicate whether there is a need to strengthen specific
areas being examined. It will also serve the purpose of discussing with
the executing agencies Bank procedures in the context of overall project
objectives and performance. Bank specialists will be invited as
necessary; and
(iii) Auditing: Auditing procedures, as well as selection and performance of
consultants will be assessed. The plan of accounts will be reviewed.
This exercise will be carried out stressing the value of appropriate
auditing as a monitoring tool to help the Government achieve the
proposed project objectives.
